border-top:#aaa 1px solid;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="display:none">\n<td colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Fatalities</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px">6,329 confirmed, 1,074 missing</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Damage</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px">$2.86 billion (2013 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>)<br />\n<small>(Preliminary total)</small></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" style="padding:0px 2px;white-space:nowrap">Areas affected</th>\n<td style="padding:0px 2px"><a href="/wiki/Caroline_Islands" title="Caroline Islands">Caroline Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_China" title="South China">South China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center; border-top:#aaa 1px solid;">Part of the <b><a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013 Pacific typhoon season</a></b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="display:none">\n<td colspan="2"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;padding:0px 2px">\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>History</b></span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Meteorological history of Typhoon Haiyan">Meteorological history</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>Response</b></span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_response_to_Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Humanitarian response to Typhoon Haiyan">Humanitarian response</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span class="noprint"><b>Other wikis</b></span></p>\n<ul>\n<li><span class="noprint"><small><a href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Typhoon_Haiyan_(2013)" class="extiw" title="commons:Category:Typhoon Haiyan (2013)">commons:Category:Typhoon Haiyan (2013)</a></small></span></li>\n</ul>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p><b>Typhoon Haiyan</b> was an extremely deadly and intense typhoon, known as <b>Super Typhoon Yolanda</b> in the Philippines. On making landfall, Haiyan devastated portions of <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It is the deadliest <a href="/wiki/Typhoons_in_the_Philippines" title="Typhoons in the Philippines">Philippine typhoon</a> on record,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> killing at least 6,300 people in that country alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Yolanda_Final_Report_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yolanda_Final_Report-3">[3]</a></sup> In terms of JTWC-estimated 1-minute sustained winds, Haiyan is tied with <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Meranti" title="Typhoon Meranti">Meranti</a> for being the strongest <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfalling</a> tropical cyclone on record. In January 2014, bodies were still being found.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The thirtieth <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named storm</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2013 Pacific typhoon season">2013 Pacific typhoon season</a>, Haiyan originated from an <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">area of low pressure</a> several hundred kilometers east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Pohnpei" title="Pohnpei">Pohnpei</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a> on November 2, 2013. Tracking generally westward, environmental conditions favored <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">tropical cyclogenesis</a> and the system developed into a tropical depression the following day. After becoming a tropical storm and attaining the name <i>Haiyan</i> at 0000 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on November 4, the system began a period of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid deepening">rapid intensification</a> that brought it to <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">typhoon</a> intensity by 1800 UTC on November 5. By November 6, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> (JTWC) assessed the system as a Category 5-equivalent super typhoon on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale</a>; the storm passed over the island of <a href="/wiki/Kayangel" title="Kayangel">Kayangel</a> in Palau shortly after attaining this strength.</p>\n<p>Thereafter, it continued to intensify; at 1200 UTC on November 7, the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) upgraded the storm\'s maximum ten-minute sustained winds to 230&#160;km/h (145&#160;mph), the highest in relation to the cyclone. The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> put the storm\'s maximum ten-minute sustained winds at 285&#160;km/h (180&#160;mph)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> prior to landfall in the central Philippines, while the <a href="/wiki/China_Meteorological_Administration" title="China Meteorological Administration">China Meteorological Administration</a> estimated the maximum two-minute sustained winds at the time to be around 78&#160;m/s (280&#160;km/h or 175&#160;mph). At the same time, the JTWC estimated the system\'s one-minute sustained winds to 315&#160;km/h (195&#160;mph), unofficially making Haiyan the strongest tropical cyclone ever observed based on wind speed, a record which would then be surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a> in 2015 at 345&#160;km/h (215&#160;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Haiyan is also tied with <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Meranti" title="Typhoon Meranti">Typhoon Meranti</a> in 2016 as the strongest tropical cyclone in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern Hemisphere</a> by 1-minute sustained winds; several others have recorded lower central pressure readings. At 20:04 <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a> on November 7, the eye of the cyclone made its first <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> in the Philippines at <a href="/wiki/Guiuan,_Eastern_Samar" title="Guiuan, Eastern Samar">Guiuan, Eastern Samar</a>. Gradually weakening, the storm made five additional landfalls in the country before emerging over the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>. Turning northwestward, the typhoon eventually struck northern <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> as a severe tropical storm on November 10. Haiyan was last noted as a tropical depression by the JMA the following day.</p>\n<p>The cyclone caused catastrophic destruction in the <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a>, particularly on <a href="/wiki/Samar_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Samar island">Samar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leyte" title="Leyte">Leyte</a>. According to UN officials, about 11 million people have been affected \xe2\x80\x93 many have been left homeless.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div class="toctitle">\n<h2>Contents</h2>\n</div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a response</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-17"><a href="#Humanitarian_crisis_and_population_displacement"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.4</span> <span class="toctext">Humanitarian crisis and population displacement</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-18"><a href="#International_response"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.5</span> <span class="toctext">International response</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-19"><a href="#Supranational_bodies"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Supranational bodies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20"><a href="#Celebrities.2C_companies.2C_and_NGOs"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.6</span> <span class="toctext">Celebrities, companies, and NGOs</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-4 tocsection-21"><a href="#Politics_involving_aid_relief"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Politics involving aid relief</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Vietnam_3"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Vietnam</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Climate_change"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Climate change</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#In_popular_media"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">In popular media</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<p></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Typhoon_Haiyan" title="Meteorological history of Typhoon Haiyan">Meteorological history of Typhoon Haiyan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haiyan_2013_track.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Haiyan_2013_track.png/300px-Haiyan_2013_track.png" width="300" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Haiyan_2013_track.png/450px-Haiyan_2013_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Haiyan_2013_track.png/600px-Haiyan_2013_track.png 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1669" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haiyan_2013_track.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>On November 2, the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Typhoon_Warning_Center" title="Joint Typhoon Warning Center">Joint Typhoon Warning Center</a> (JTWC) began monitoring a broad <a href="/wiki/Low-pressure_area" title="Low-pressure area">low-pressure area</a> about 425 kilometers (265 miles) east-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Pohnpei" title="Pohnpei">Pohnpei</a>, one of the states in the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[nb 1]</a></sup> As the system moved through a region favoring <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">tropical cyclogenesis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a> (JMA) classified it as a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_depression" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical depression">tropical depression</a> early on November 3.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[nb 2]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The system quickly intensified into a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storm</a>, prompting the JMA to <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">assign it the name</a> <i>Haiyan</i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh" xml:lang="zh">\xe6\xb5\xb7\xe7\x87\x95</span>; literally: "<a href="/wiki/Petrel" title="Petrel">petrel</a>") at 0000 UTC on November 4.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup> Tracking generally westward along the southern periphery of a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" class="mw-redirect" title="Rapid deepening">rapid intensification</a> ensued by November 5 as a <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> with an embedded <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> developing; the JMA classified Haiyan as a typhoon later that day.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup> On November 6, the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration</a> (PAGASA) assigned the storm the local name <i>Yolanda</i> as it approached their <a href="/wiki/Area_of_responsibility" title="Area of responsibility">area of responsibility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Intensification slowed somewhat during the day, though the JTWC estimated the storm to have attained <a href="/wiki/SSHS#Category_5" class="mw-redirect" title="SSHS">Category 5-equivalent</a> super typhoon status on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson hurricane wind scale</a> around 1200 UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-STY_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STY-17">[nb 3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup> Later, the eye of the typhoon passed over the island of <a href="/wiki/Kayangel" title="Kayangel">Kayangel</a> in Palau.<sup id="cite_ref-palau_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palau-19">[16]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png/220px-Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png/330px-Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png/440px-Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="699" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Comparison_between_Haiyan_and_Katrina.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nComparison between Haiyan and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Katrina</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Around 1200 UTC on November 7, Haiyan attained ten-minute sustained winds of 230&#160;km/h (145&#160;mph) and a minimum <a href="/wiki/Barometric_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Barometric pressure">central pressure</a> of 895 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 26.43 <a href="/wiki/Inches_of_Mercury" class="mw-redirect" title="Inches of Mercury">inHg</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup> Six hours later, the JTWC estimated Haiyan to have attained one-minute sustained winds of 315&#160;km/h (195&#160;mph) and gusts up to 380&#160;km/h (235&#160;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-JTWC-PR19_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC-PR19-20">[17]</a></sup> The storm displayed some characteristics of an <a href="/wiki/Annular_tropical_cyclone" title="Annular tropical cyclone">annular tropical cyclone</a>, though a strong convective band remained present along the western side of the system.<sup id="cite_ref-JTWC-PR19_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC-PR19-20">[17]</a></sup></p>\n<p>At 2040 UTC on November 7, Typhoon Haiyan made <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guiuan" class="mw-redirect" title="Guiuan">Guiuan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Samar" title="Eastern Samar">Eastern Samar</a> at peak intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-webcitation1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webcitation1-21">[18]</a></sup> The JTWC\'s unofficial estimate of one-minute sustained winds of 305&#160;km/h (190&#160;mph) would, by that measure, make Haiyan the most powerful storm ever recorded to strike land.<sup id="cite_ref-JeffMNov7_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JeffMNov7-22">[19]</a></sup> Interaction with land caused slight degradation of the storm\'s structure, though it remained an exceptionally powerful storm when it struck <a href="/wiki/Tolosa,_Leyte" title="Tolosa, Leyte">Tolosa, Leyte</a> around 2300 UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> The typhoon made four additional landfalls as it traversed the Visayas:<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daanbantayan,_Cebu" class="mw-redirect" title="Daanbantayan, Cebu">Daanbantayan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bantayan_Island" title="Bantayan Island">Bantayan Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concepcion,_Iloilo" title="Concepcion, Iloilo">Concepcion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Busuanga_Island" title="Busuanga Island">Busuanga Island</a>.</p>\n<p>Haiyan, with its core disrupted by interaction with the Philippines, emerged over the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> late on November 8.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> Environmental conditions ahead of the storm soon became less favorable, as cool stable air began wrapping into the western side of the circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> Continuing across the South China Sea, Haiyan turned more northwesterly late on November 9 and through November 10 as it moved around the southwestern edge of the subtropical ridge previously steering it westward.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> Rapid weakening ensued as Haiyan approached its final landfall in Vietnam,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> ultimately striking the country near <a href="/wiki/Haiphong" title="Haiphong">Haiphong</a> around 2100 UTC as a severe tropical storm.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup> Once onshore, the storm quickly diminished and was last noted as it dissipated over <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi Province</a>, China, on November 11.<sup id="cite_ref-Haiyan_BT_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haiyan_BT-11">[10]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">Preparations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Preparations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Micronesia_and_Palau">Micronesia and Palau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Micronesia and Palau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png/220px-Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png/330px-Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png/440px-Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haiyan_2013-11-06_0225Z.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTyphoon Haiyan near Palau on November 6</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Upon JTWC\'s declaration of Tropical Depression 31W on November 3, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm warning</a> was issued for <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_Lagoon" title="Chuuk Lagoon">Chuuk Lagoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Losap" title="Losap">Losap</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Poluwat" title="Poluwat">Poluwat</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Federated States of Micronesia</a>. Further west, <a href="/wiki/Faraulep" title="Faraulep">Faraulep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satawal" title="Satawal">Satawal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Woleai" title="Woleai">Woleai</a>, were placed under a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">typhoon watch</a> while <a href="/wiki/Fananu" title="Fananu">Fananu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ulul" title="Ulul">Ulul</a> were placed under a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical storm watch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> The following day, the tropical storm warning expanded to include Satawal while a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">typhoon warning</a> was issued for Woleai.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> Much of <a href="/wiki/Yap_State" title="Yap State">Yap State</a> and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Koror" title="Koror">Koror</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kayangel" title="Kayangel">Kayangel</a> in Palau were placed under a typhoon watch.<sup id="cite_ref-haiyan_advisory_6_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haiyan_advisory_6-31">[28]</a></sup> The government issued a mandatory evacuation for Kayangel, and although most residents ignored the warning, they all survived the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-palau_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palau-19">[16]</a></sup> As Haiyan progressed westward, the easternmost advisories were gradually discontinued.<sup id="cite_ref-haiyan_advisory_6_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haiyan_advisory_6-31">[28]</a></sup> As Haiyan intensified into a typhoon on November 5, warnings were raised across Palau and Yap State.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> Government offices in <a href="/wiki/Melekeok" title="Melekeok">Melekeok</a> were used as an evacuation building for Palau.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha117_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha117-34">[31]</a></sup> Despite mandatory evacuation orders, most residents on Kayangel remained on the island and rode out the typhoon.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC1-35">[32]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YolandaRainfallWarning.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YolandaRainfallWarning.png/220px-YolandaRainfallWarning.png" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YolandaRainfallWarning.png/330px-YolandaRainfallWarning.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/YolandaRainfallWarning.png/440px-YolandaRainfallWarning.png 2x" data-file-width="745" data-file-height="788" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YolandaRainfallWarning.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPAGASA raised rainfall warning advisory in the Central and Eastern Visayas during the passage of Haiyan (Yolanda).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Shortly before Typhoon Haiyan entered the Philippine Area of Responsibility on November 6, PAGASA raised <a href="/wiki/Typhoons_in_the_Philippines#Public_Storm_Warning_Signals" title="Typhoons in the Philippines">Public Storm Warning Signal</a> (PSWS) No.1, the lowest of four levels, for much of the <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">Mindanao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> As the storm continued to approach the country, warnings expanded into <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">Luzon</a> and increased in severity for eastern areas.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> By the evening of November 7, PSWS No. 4, the highest level of warning which indicates winds in excess of 185&#160;km/h (115&#160;mph) are expected, was raised for <a href="/wiki/Biliran_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Biliran Island">Biliran Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Samar" title="Eastern Samar">Eastern Samar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leyte_(province)" title="Leyte (province)">Leyte</a>, Northern <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_Cebu" title="Metro Cebu">Metro Cebu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Leyte" title="Southern Leyte">Southern Leyte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> Through November 8, the coverage of PSWS No. 4 continued to expand, with areas in southern Luzon being included.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png/220px-Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png/330px-Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png/440px-Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1982" data-file-height="1705" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yolanda_PSWS_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nPSWS Map in the Philippines during the passage of Typhoon Haiyan (Yolanda).</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Officials placed police officers in the <a href="/wiki/Bicol_Region" title="Bicol Region">Bicol Region</a> ahead of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup> In the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leyte" title="Leyte">Leyte</a>, classes were canceled, and residents in flood- and landslide-prone areas were required to evacuate.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> Some of the storm-threatened areas were affected by an earlier <a href="/wiki/2013_Bohol_earthquake" title="2013 Bohol earthquake">earthquake in Bohol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> Then-Philippine President <a href="/wiki/Noynoy_Aquino" class="mw-redirect" title="Noynoy Aquino">Noynoy Aquino</a> requested the military to deploy planes and helicopters to the region expected to be affected.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> As Haiyan was moving very fast, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> issued warnings at different levels to about 60 of the 80 provinces, including the capital <a href="/wiki/Metro_Manila" title="Metro Manila">Metro Manila</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> On November 8, the <a href="/wiki/International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters" title="International Charter on Space and Major Disasters">International Charter on Space and Major Disasters</a> was activated, providing widespread charitable satellite coverage to relief organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_China">Southern China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Southern China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The State Flood Control and Drought Relief Headquarters hoisted a level three emergency response in the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>, Guangdong and <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a>. All fishing vessels were urged to return to ports by noon on November 9.<sup id="cite_ref-english.peopledaily.com.cn_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-english.peopledaily.com.cn-47">[44]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> issued the Strong Monsoon Signal at 19:10 HKT on November 9,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> and it was still in place on November 13.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On November 8, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nguyen_Tan_Dung" class="mw-redirect" title="Nguyen Tan Dung">Nguyen Tan Dung</a> activated the highest state of preparedness in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-VietnameRW1_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VietnameRW1-50">[47]</a></sup> Approximately 600,000 people across southern and central provinces were evacuated while a further 200,000 were evacuated in northern provinces. Alerts were sent to 85,328 seagoing vessels, with a collective crew of 385,372 people, to sail to safer waters away from the storm. Requests were sent to China, Malaysia, Indonesia, and the Philippines to aid any fishermen who needed immediate shelter from the typhoon.<sup id="cite_ref-VietnamRW2_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VietnamRW2-51">[48]</a></sup> Threatening Vietnam after two other typhoons, <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Wutip_(2013)" title="Typhoon Wutip (2013)">Wutip</a> and <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nari_(2013)" title="Typhoon Nari (2013)">Nari</a>, there were concerns that the storm would cause significant damage to homes with makeshift repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> Roughly 460,000 military personnel and other authorities were mobilized to assist in evacuation efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-VietnamRW2_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VietnamRW2-51">[48]</a></sup> Hundreds of flights were canceled across the country while schools were closed on November 11. On the small island of <a href="/wiki/C%E1%BB%93n_C%E1%BB%8F_District" title="C\xe1\xbb\x93n C\xe1\xbb\x8f District">C\xe1\xbb\x93n C\xe1\xbb\x8f</a>, all residents were moved to underground shelters with enough supplies for several days.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCNov10_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNov10-53">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Societies" title="International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies">International Federation of Red Cross and Red Crescent Societies</a> (IFRC) branches in Vietnam prepared relief stockpiles, consisting of food, water, housing material, and <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_%C4%91%E1%BB%93ng" title="Vietnamese \xc4\x91\xe1\xbb\x93ng">\xe2\x82\xab</a>6.6 billion (US$310,000) in funds.<sup id="cite_ref-VietnamRW2_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VietnamRW2-51">[48]</a></sup> The local United Nations Resident Coordinator, Pratibha Mehta, praised the government\'s actions and credited them with saving numerous lives.<sup id="cite_ref-VietnameRW1_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VietnameRW1-50">[47]</a></sup> However, there were complaints from many residents that the warnings came too late.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCNov10_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCNov10-53">[50]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" border="1" style="float: right; margin:0 1em 0.5em 1em;">\n<caption>Fatalities by country</caption>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Country</b></td>\n<td><b>Deaths</b></td>\n<td><b>Missing</b></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a></td>\n<td>6,300</td>\n<td>1,061</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></td>\n<td>11</td>\n<td>9</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a></td>\n<td>10</td>\n<td>4</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a></td>\n<td>8</td>\n<td>0</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Total</b></td>\n<td><b>6,329</b></td>\n<td><b>1,074</b></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Micronesia_and_Palau_2">Micronesia and Palau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Micronesia and Palau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On Kayangel in Palau, a high <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surge</a> damaged several houses,<sup id="cite_ref-ocha117_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha117-34">[31]</a></sup> while strong winds downed trees.<sup id="cite_ref-palau_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palau-19">[16]</a></sup> Despite residents\' refusal to evacuate, no fatalities or major injuries took place on the island. Helicopters were flown to the island to survey damage and provide relief supplies. The government planned to evacuate those who were left homeless from the island.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC1_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC1-35">[32]</a></sup> Koror, <a href="/wiki/Babeldaob" title="Babeldaob">Babeldaob</a> and Kayangel each lost access to water and power.<sup id="cite_ref-palau_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-palau-19">[16]</a></sup> In Koror, winds reaching as high as 120&#160;km/h (75&#160;mph) blew out rooftops and downed trees and power lines. A causeway linking an offshore hospital to the main island was temporarily shut down after being inundated by water.<sup id="cite_ref-OCHAFlashUpdate3_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCHAFlashUpdate3-54">[51]</a></sup> On the northern end of Babeldaob, Haiyan damaged schools and buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha117_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha117-34">[31]</a></sup> Lying closest to Haiyan at the time of the typhoon\'s passage, Kayangel was flooded in its entirety, and all homes were destroyed. Though no people were killed there, 69 others were displaced by the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-OCHAFlashUpdate3_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCHAFlashUpdate3-54">[51]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines_2">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation">\n<tr>\n<td class="mbox-image">\n<div LANDO (KOPPU)</a></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr style="text-align:right;">\n<td colspan="5">\n<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n<ul>\n<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Costliest_Philippine_typhoons" title="Template talk:Costliest Philippine typhoons"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Costliest_Philippine_typhoons&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<hr />\n<table class="infobox collapsible collapsed" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em; width:30em;">\n<tr>\n<th colspan="4" class="sortkey">7003126800000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>1,268</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>10</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Trix_(1952)" class="mw-redirect" title="Typhoon Trix (1952)">Trix</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1952_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1952 Pacific typhoon season">1952</a></td>\n<td><span style="display:none" class="sortkey">7002995000000000000\xe2\x99\xa0</span>995</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="4">\n<hr /></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4">\n<dl>\n<dt>Sources</dt>\n</dl>\n<div class="refbegin" style="">\n<ol>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://blog.noah.dost.gov.ph/wp-content/uploads/2013/11/Storm-Surge-Timeline-Infographic-23-Nov-2013-big.png">Philippine Storm Surge History</a> by Project NOAH of PAGASA.</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.abs-cbnnews.com/focus/11/08/13/deadliest-typhoons-philippines">Deadliest typhoons in the Philippines</a> article published by ABS-CBN News on November 8, 2013.</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.typhoon2000.ph/stormstats/WorstPhilippineTyphoons.htm">Worst Typhoons in the Philippines</a> according to Typhoon 2000.</li>\n<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ndrrmc.gov.ph/attachments/article/1177/Update%20Effects%20TY%20YOLANDA%2017%20April%202014.pdf">NDRRMC Updates re Effects of TY YOLANDA (HAIYAN)</a> by the NDRRMC on April 15, 2014.</li>\n<li><cite class="citation journal">Pedro Ribera, Ricardo Garcia-Herrera and Luis Gimeno (July 2008). "Historical deadly typhoons in the Philippines". <i>Weather</i>. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Meteorological_Society" title="Royal Meteorological Society">Royal Meteorological Society</a>. <b>63</b> (7): 196. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1002%2Fwea.275">10.1002/wea.275</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATyphoon+Haiyan&amp;rft.atitle=Historical+deadly+typhoons+in+the+Philippines&amp;rft.au=Pedro+Ribera%2C+Ricardo+Garcia-Herrera+and+Luis+Gimeno&amp;rft.date=2008-07&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.issue=7&amp;rft.jtitle=Weather&amp;rft.pages=196&amp;rft.volume=63&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1002%2Fwea.275&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>\n</ol>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="4" style="text-align:right;">\n<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">\n<ul>\n<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Deadliest_Philippine_Typhoons" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Deadliest Philippine Typhoons"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Deadliest_Philippine_Typhoons&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:Deadliest Philippine Typhoons (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>\n<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Deadliest_Philippine_Typhoons&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<p>Typhoon Haiyan, called Typhoon Yolanda in the Philippines, caused catastrophic damage throughout much of the islands of <a href="/wiki/Leyte_(province)" title="Leyte (province)">Leyte</a>, where cities and towns were largely destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribuneNov13_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribuneNov13-57">[53]</a></sup> As of April 17, 2016, the <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Risk_Reduction_and_Management_Council" title="National Disaster Risk Reduction and Management Council">National Disaster Risk Reduction and Management Council</a> (NDRRMC) confirmed 6,300 fatalities across the country, 5,877 of those taking place in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Visayas" title="Eastern Visayas">Eastern Visayas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yolanda_Final_Report_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yolanda_Final_Report-3">[3]</a></sup> The true death toll remains unclear, being claimed to be at least 10,000 by some victims from <a href="/wiki/Tacloban_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Tacloban City">Tacloban City</a>, Leyte. As of November 13, 2015, the Philippine Red Cross estimated that 22,000 people were missing.</p>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Surigao_City" title="Surigao City">Surigao City</a>, 281.9&#160;mm (11.10&#160;in) of rainfall was recorded, much of which fell in under 12 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">Storm surges</a> were also recorded in many places. In the island of <a href="/wiki/Leyte" title="Leyte">Leyte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Atmospheric,_Geophysical_and_Astronomical_Services_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Philippine Atmospheric, Geophysical and Astronomical Services Administration">PAGASA</a> measured 5\xe2\x80\x936 meter (15\xe2\x80\x9319&#160;ft) waves.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[55]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Tacloban" title="Tacloban">Tacloban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leyte" title="Leyte">Leyte</a>, the terminal building of <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Z._Romualdez_Airport" title="Daniel Z. Romualdez Airport">Tacloban Airport</a> was destroyed by a 5.2&#160;m (17&#160;ft) storm surge up to the height of the second story.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[56]</a></sup> Along the airport, a storm surge of 4&#160;m (13&#160;ft) was estimated.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> Waves of 4.6&#160;m (15&#160;ft) were also estimated.<sup id="cite_ref-world-asia-24878801_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-asia-24878801-62">[58]</a></sup> On the western coast of Samar, the storm surge was not as significant.<sup id="cite_ref-noah_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noah-63">[59]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Haiyan\'s first landfall was at Guiuan in Eastern Samar, where the typhoon touched down at 4:40am.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EverythingGoneGuiuan_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EverythingGoneGuiuan-65">[61]</a></sup> Nearly all structures in the township suffered at least partial damage, many of which were completely flattened.<sup id="cite_ref-EasternSamarIsolated_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EasternSamarIsolated-66">[62]</a></sup> For several days following Haiyan\'s first landfall, the damage situation in the fishing town remained unclear due to lack of communication in and out of the area.<sup id="cite_ref-YolandaCutsSwath_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YolandaCutsSwath-67">[63]</a></sup> The damage could finally be assessed after <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Air_Force" title="Philippine Air Force">Philippine Air Force</a> staff arrived in Guiuan on November 10.<sup id="cite_ref-YolandaFlatensGuiuan_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YolandaFlatensGuiuan-68">[64]</a></sup> Prior to this, a local priest was able to take his motorbike from Guiuan to the towns of Cabalogan and Calbayog (also in Samar) armed with photos of the devastation, shot on his mobile phone.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup></p>\n<p>There was widespread devastation from the storm surge in Tacloban City especially in San Jose, with many buildings being destroyed, trees knocked over or broken, and cars piled up.<sup id="cite_ref-world-asia-24878801_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-asia-24878801-62">[58]</a></sup> The low-lying areas on the eastern side of Tacloban city were hardest hit, with some areas completely washed away. Flooding also extended for 1&#160;km (0.62&#160;mi) inland on the east coast of the province.<sup id="cite_ref-world-asia-24878801_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-asia-24878801-62">[58]</a></sup> City administrator Tecson John Lim stated that roughly 90 percent of the city had been destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribuneNov13_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribuneNov13-57">[53]</a></sup> Journalists on the ground have described the devastation as, "off the scale, and apocalyptic".<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-70">[66]</a></sup> Most families in Samar and Leyte lost some family members or relatives; families came in from outlying provinces looking for relatives, especially children, who may have been washed away.<sup id="cite_ref-typhoon-haiyan-dead-aid_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-typhoon-haiyan-dead-aid-71">[67]</a></sup> The entire first floor of the <a href="/wiki/Tacloban_City_Convention_Center" title="Tacloban City Convention Center">Tacloban City Convention Center</a>, which was serving as an evacuation shelter, was submerged by storm surge. Many residents in the building were caught off-guard by the fast rising waters and subsequently drowned or were injured in the building.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Although wind speeds were extreme, the major cause of damage and loss of life appears to have been storm surge. The major focus of devastation appears to have been on the east coast of Samar and Leyte, with a particular focus on Tacloban, because of its location between Samar and Leyte, and the large population in low-lying areas.<sup id="cite_ref-noah_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noah-63">[59]</a></sup> Philippine <a href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Interior_and_Local_Government" title="Department of the Interior and Local Government">Department of the Interior and Local Government</a> (DILG) <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Interior_and_Local_Government_(Philippines)" title="Secretary of the Interior and Local Government (Philippines)">Secretary</a> Mar Roxas said the scale of the relief operation that was now required was overwhelming, with some places described as a wasteland of mud and debris.<sup id="cite_ref-world-asia-24887746_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-asia-24887746-73">[69]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Sebastian Rhodes Stampa, head of a UN disaster assessment co-ordination team, said there was "destruction on a massive scale" in Tacloban. "There are cars thrown like tumbleweed and the streets are strewn with debris. The last time I saw something of this scale was in the aftermath of the [2004] Indian Ocean tsunami."<sup id="cite_ref-world-asia-24878801_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-world-asia-24878801-62">[58]</a></sup> There is little communication in the city, and no mobile phone coverage. Up the east coast of the Leyte there are numerous towns and villages that are completely cut off without any assistance. Large parts of Leyte and Samar are without power and may have no power for a month.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-70">[66]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The storm crossed the <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a> region for almost a day, causing widespread flooding. In <a href="/wiki/Cebu" title="Cebu">Cebu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bohol" title="Bohol">Bohol</a>, struck by a magnitude 7.2 <a href="/wiki/2013_Bohol_earthquake" title="2013 Bohol earthquake">earthquake</a> two weeks before, cities were also severely devastated.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> During the morning of November 8, media stations across the country were able to broadcast live the destruction of Haiyan. However, before afternoon, all communications on the <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a> region failed. The Presidential Communications Department of President <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">Benigno Aquino III</a> had difficulty contacting DILG Secretary <a href="/wiki/Mar_Roxas" title="Mar Roxas">Mar Roxas</a> and Defense Secretary <a href="/wiki/Voltaire_Gazmin" title="Voltaire Gazmin">Voltaire Gazmin</a> in Tacloban City to plan relief.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup> Widespread power interruptions, landslides and flash floods were also reported. Major roads were blocked by trees, and impassable. 453 domestic and international airline flights were canceled. Some airports were also closed on November 8 and 9. Ferries were affected. Relief and rescue efforts were underway by November 9, but some places remained isolated and out of communication due to severe damage.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China_and_Taiwan">China and Taiwan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: China and Taiwan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Typhoon Haiyan reached <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Hainan Province">Hainan Province</a>, where severe damage took place and six people were killed in various incidents.<sup id="cite_ref-CRINov12_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRINov12-77">[73]</a></sup> The hardest hit area was <a href="/wiki/Qionghai" title="Qionghai">Qionghai</a>, where roughly 3,500 people across 20 villages were isolated due to extensive flooding.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[74]</a></sup> Direct economic losses in Hainan amounted to <a href="/wiki/Chinese_yuan" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese yuan">\xc2\xa5</a>4.9 billion (US$803 million).<sup id="cite_ref-CRINov12_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRINov12-77">[73]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Guangxi_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Guangxi Province">Guangxi Province</a> to the north, heavy rains up to 380&#160;mm (15&#160;in) fell and wind gusts reached 100&#160;km/h (60&#160;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-ABCNov12_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNov12-79">[75]</a></sup> An estimated 1.21 million people were affected, of whom 26,300 were evacuated. Two people died while four others went missing after a car fell off a flooded road into a river near <a href="/wiki/Beihai" title="Beihai">Beihai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[76]</a></sup> Losses throughout Guangxi amounted to \xc2\xa5275 million (US$45 million).<sup id="cite_ref-CRINov12_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRINov12-77">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABCNov12_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNov12-79">[75]</a></sup> Approximately 900 homes and 25,500 hectares of crops were destroyed, while 8,500 homes were damaged. Additionally, an estimated 3 million people were affected by the storm throughout Southern China.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[77]</a></sup> A cargo ship broke moorings at <a href="/wiki/Sanya" title="Sanya">Sanya</a> on November 8;<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua132876092_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua132876092-82">[78]</a></sup> three members of the crew drowned while four others went missing.<sup id="cite_ref-ABCNov12_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNov12-79">[75]</a></sup> One person also went missing off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Lantau_Island" title="Lantau Island">Lantau Island</a>, Hong Kong.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[79]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Along the coast of <a href="/wiki/New_Taipei_City" title="New Taipei City">New Taipei</a>, 16 people were swept out to sea by three 8&#160;m (26&#160;ft) waves. After several hours of search and rescue, eight were hospitalized while the other eight drowned. This was considered the largest loss of life from waves in Taiwan in several years.<sup id="cite_ref-Xinhua132875773_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Xinhua132875773-84">[80]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam_2">Vietnam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Vietnam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Haiyan made landfall as a severe tropical storm in <a href="/wiki/Qu%E1%BA%A3ng_Ninh_Province" title="Qu\xe1\xba\xa3ng Ninh Province">Qu\xe1\xba\xa3ng Ninh Province</a> on November 10 and produced high winds and widespread heavy rainfall which affected northern Vietnam.<sup id="cite_ref-Vietnam_Member_Report_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vietnam_Member_Report-85">[81]</a></sup> Rainfall totals of up to 461&#160;mm (18.1&#160;in) and wind gusts of up to 147&#160;km/h (91&#160;mph) were recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-Vietnam_Member_Report_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vietnam_Member_Report-85">[81]</a></sup> Ten people were killed while they were preparing for Haiyan\'s landfall, while no one was killed after the system made landfall; however, 4 people are missing in Qu\xe1\xba\xa3ng Ninh Province.<sup id="cite_ref-Vietnam_Member_Report_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vietnam_Member_Report-85">[81]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Due to extensive damage and high death toll, PAGASA announced that the name <i>Yolanda</i> would be stricken off the typhoon naming lists.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup> PAGASA chose the name <i>Yasmin</i> to replace <i>Yolanda</i> for the <a href="/wiki/2017_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2017 Pacific typhoon season">2017 season</a>. During their 2014 annual session the ESCAP/WMO Typhoon Committee announced that the name <i>Haiyan</i> would also be retired from its naming lists on January 1, 2015, and was therefore replaced by the name <i>Bailu</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines_3">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Philippines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Visayas,_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Visayas%2C_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif/220px-Visayas%2C_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Visayas%2C_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif/330px-Visayas%2C_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif 1.5x, data-file-width="1415" data-file-height="979" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Visayas,_Philippines_power_outage_before_and_after_Haiyan_2013.gif" data-file-width="1753" data-file-height="1240" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ReliefNet_Map_of_Damaged_houses_Typhoon_Haiyan.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMap of damaged houses by municipality showing track of storm, from the United Nations, as of November 18, 2013</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg/220px-Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg/330px-Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg/440px-Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Damayan_131118-M-LT992-019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAn aerial view of <a href="/wiki/Guiuan,_Eastern_Samar" title="Guiuan, Eastern Samar">Guiuan</a>, the town where the typhoon made its first landfall</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG/220px-Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG/330px-Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG/440px-Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Basey_after_Yolanda.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nDestruction in <a href="/wiki/Basey,_Samar" title="Basey, Samar">Basey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samar" title="Samar">Samar</a> after the typhoon passed over the town.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>By November 11, the provinces of Aklan, Capiz, Cebu, Iloilo, Leyte, Palawan, and Samar, were placed under a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of national calamity</a>, allowing the government to use state funds for relief and rehabilitation and to control prices of basic goods.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup> Additionally, approximately \xe2\x82\xb130.6 million (US$700,000) had been allocated in relief assistance by the NDRRMC. Local and national agencies deployed a collective 18,177 personnel, 844 vehicles, 44 seagoing vessels, and 31 aircraft for various operations.<sup id="cite_ref-Yolanda_Final_Report_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yolanda_Final_Report-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Bishops%27_Conference_of_the_Philippines" title="Catholic Bishops\' Conference of the Philippines">CBCP</a> also declared 8 days of mourning for victims of the typhoon on the same date.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[86]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> Representative in the Philippines Dr <a href="/wiki/Julie_Hall" title="Julie Hall">Julie Hall</a> noted that while many survivors requiring medical attention in the first week suffer from trauma and fractures, the concern shifts toward chronic conditions as the weeks pass. The WHO coordinated the massive international response to help the Philippine government meet the acute need for healthcare services in the affected areas.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[87]</a></sup></p>\n<p>Extreme damage to infrastructure throughout the region posed logistical problems that greatly slowed relief efforts. Though aid was flown into local airports, most of it remained there as roads remained closed.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[88]</a></sup> According to estimates on November 13, only 20 percent of the affected population in Tacloban City was receiving aid. With lack of access to clean water, some residents dug up water pipes and boiled water from there in order to survive. Thousands of people sought to evacuate the city via <a href="/wiki/C-130" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130">C-130</a> cargo planes, however, the slow process fueled further aggravation. Reports of escaped prisoners <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">raping</a> women in the city prompted a further urgency to evacuate. One resident was quoted as saying "Tacloban is a dead city."<sup id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribuneNov13_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribuneNov13-57">[53]</a></sup> Due to the lack of electricity, planes could only operate during the daylight, further slowing the evacuations. At dawn on November 12, thousands of people broke through fences and rushed planes only to be forced back by police and military personnel. A similar incident occurred later that day as a U.S. cargo plane was landing.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimesNov12_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimesNov12-93">[89]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On November 14, a correspondent from the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> reported Tacloban to be a "war zone," although the situation soon stabilized when the presence of government law enforcement was increased. Safety concerns prompted several relief agencies to back out of the operation, and some United Nations staff were pulled out for safety reasons. A message circulating among the agencies urged them to not go into Tacloban for this reason.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[90]</a></sup> On the west coast of Leyte Island, residents in <a href="/wiki/Ormoc" title="Ormoc">Ormoc</a> were fearing that the focus on Tacloban City would leave them without aid. Though not as hard hit, roughly 90 percent of the city was damaged or destroyed and supplies were running low. Hospitals in the city were either shut down or working at partial capacity, leaving many of the nearly 2,000 injured in the city without medical assistance. In nearby <a href="/wiki/Baybay" title="Baybay">Baybay</a>, lack of assistance fueled anger and incited looting for survival.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[91]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In the coastal community Guiuan, which took the full brunt of the typhoon, Mayor Christopher Gonzalez is credited with saving countless lives after he incessantly urged residents to evacuate. He referred to the storm as "delubyo (deluge)," which roughly translates to Armageddon. Of the town\'s 45,000 residents, 87 died, 931 were injured, and 23 others were listed as missing. U.S. Navy Capt. Russell Hays, a medical officer, estimated that a storm of Haiyan\'s caliber could have killed as many as 4,500 in Guiuan alone had it not been for the mayor\'s efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup></p>\n<p>On November 18, the government of the Philippines launched an online portal, called the Foreign Aid Transparency Hub (FaiTH), that provides the public a transparency view of the funds and other aids received by the government from the international community.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup></p>\n<p>To lead the management and rehabilitation efforts of the central provinces in the Philippines affected by Typhoon Haiyan, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> President <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">Benigno Aquino III</a> appointed <a href="/wiki/Panfilo_Lacson" title="Panfilo Lacson">Panfilo Lacson</a> as Typhoon Haiyan Rehabilation Czar.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-99">[95]</a></sup></p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_impact">Environmental impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Typhoon_Haiyan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environmental impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marine_Corps_HC-130_Hercules_aircraft_assigned_to_the_3rd_Marine_Expeditionary_Brigade_and_other_military_aircraft_sit_on_the_tarmac_at_an_airport_in_Guiuan,_Philippines,_waiting_to_airlift_Philippine_131117-N-XN177-381.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/U.S._Marine_Corps_HC-130_Hercules_aircraft_assigned_to_the_3rd_Marine_Expeditionary_Brigade_and_other_military_aircraft_sit_on_the_tarmac_at_an_airport_in_Guiuan%2C_Philippines%2C_waiting_to_airlift_Philippine_131117-N-XN177-381.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg"
